<tr style="display:none">\n        <td colspan="2">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n         <p>\n          <a class="image" Hurley, Payette, Polansky, Marshburn, and Kopra\n         <div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n           Space Shuttle program\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div style="width:100%">\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: left; text-align:left;padding-right:0.5em;">\n           \xe2\x86\x90\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n            STS-125\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;">\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-128" title="STS-128">\n            STS-128\n           </a>\n           \xe2\x86\x92\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        STS-127\n       </b>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_International_Space_Station" title="Assembly of the International Space Station">\n        ISS assembly\n       </a>\n       flight\n       <b>\n        2J/A\n       </b>\n       ) was a\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       mission to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ql1_1-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ql1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It was the twenty-third flight of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n        <i>\n         Endeavour\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       . The primary purpose of the STS-127 mission was to deliver and install the final two components of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">\n        Japanese Experiment Module\n       </a>\n       : the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module#Exposed_Facility" title="Japanese Experiment Module">\n        Exposed Facility\n       </a>\n       (JEM EF), and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module#Experiment_Logistics_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">\n        Exposed Section\n       </a>\n       of the Experiment Logistics Module (ELM-ES).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boeing_3-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-boeing-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       When\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       docked with the ISS on this mission in July 2009, it set a record for the most humans in space at the same time in the same vehicle, the first time thirteen people have been at the station at the same time.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fuels_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fuels-5">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It also tied the record of thirteen people in space at any one time.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The first launch attempt, on 13 June 2009, was scrubbed due to a gaseous hydrogen leak observed during tanking.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub1_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-scrub1-6">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-second_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-second-7">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate (GUCP) on the external fuel tank experienced a potentially hazardous hydrogen gas leak similar to the fault that delayed the\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n         Space Shuttle\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       mission\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-119" title="STS-119">\n        STS-119\n       </a>\n       in March 2009. Since a launch date of 18 June 2009 would have conflicted with the launch of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">\n        Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter\n       </a>\n       (LRO)/Lunar Crater Observation and Sensing Satellite (LCROSS), NASA managers discussed the scheduling conflict with both the Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter project and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Force_Eastern_Range" title="Air Force Eastern Range">\n        Air Force Eastern Range\n       </a>\n       , which provides tracking support for rockets launched from Florida.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub3_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-scrub3-8">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A decision was made to allow the shuttle to attempt a second launch on 17 June 2009, allowing LRO to launch on 18 June 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-second_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-second-7">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The second launch attempt on 17 June 2009 was also scrubbed due to hydrogen leak issues seen from the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ground_Umbilical_Carrier_Plate" title="Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate">\n        Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub17_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-scrub17-10">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Due to conflicts with the launch of the LRO, and due to a\n       <a href="/wiki/Beta_angle" title="Beta angle">\n        beta angle\n       </a>\n       constraint, the next available launch opportunity was scheduled for 11 July 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schedule_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-schedule-11">\n         [NASA 2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-window_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-window-12">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A successful tanking test for leak checks was performed on 1 July 2009, with modified GUCP seals allowing launch preparations to proceed as scheduled.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Because of lightning strikes near the launch pad during the evening of 10 July 2009, NASA scrubbed the launch for the third time and rescheduled for 12 July 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Due to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Return_To_Launch_Site" title="Return To Launch Site">\n        Return To Launch Site\n       </a>\n       (RTLS) weather violation, NASA scrubbed the launch for the fourth time on the evening of 12 July 2009.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       STS-127\'s fifth launch attempt, on 13 July 2009, was also scrubbed due to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anvil_cloud" title="Anvil cloud">\n        anvil clouds\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">\n        lightning\n       </a>\n       within 10 nautical miles (19\xc2\xa0km) of the launch site, which violated launch safety rules. STS-127 finally launched successfully on its sixth launch attempt, on 15 July 2009 at 18:03 EDT. Pieces of foam were observed falling off of the External Tank during the ascent, the same occurrence that had led to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        loss of\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       in 2003. However,\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       only received minor scuffs to its heat shield, the damage not enough to cause concern over reentry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts127heatshield_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts127heatshield-15">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The shuttle landed at\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       16 days later at 10:48 EDT on 31 July 2009.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n href="/wiki/List_of_space_travelers_by_name" title="List of space travelers by name">\n           person to fly in space\n          </a>\n          .\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-500th_17-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-500th-17">\n            [14]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </p>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_payload">\n        Mission payload\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-127&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Mission payload">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="2000" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg/220px-Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg/330px-Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg/440px-Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Endeavour_payload_bay.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Payload bay of the shuttle being loaded.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="837" data-file-width="566" height="325" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg/220px-12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg/330px-12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg/440px-12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:12_ICC-VLD1_STS-127.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         ICC-VLD1 STS-127\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       carried a wide variety of equipment and cargo in the payload bay, with the largest item being the\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       Japanese Experiment Module Exposed Facility (JEM EF), and the\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       Japanese Experiment Logistics Module \xe2\x80\x93 Exposed Section (ELM-ES).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The exposed facility is a part of\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       that will allow astronauts to perform science experiments that are exposed to the vacuum of space. The exposed section is similar to the logistics module on the\n       <i>\n        Kibo\n       </i>\n       laboratory, but is not pressurized.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Once its payloads were transferred to the JEM EF, the ELM-ES was returned to the payload bay.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Also inside the payload bay was an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integrated_Cargo_Carrier" title="Integrated Cargo Carrier">\n        Integrated Cargo Carrier\n       </a>\n       -Vertical Light Deployable (ICC-VLD), containing a variety of equipment and spare components for the station. The carrier contained six new batteries for installation on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S6_truss" title="S6 truss">\n        P6 truss\n       </a>\n       , that was installed during two of the mission\'s spacewalks, as well as a spare space-to-ground antenna and a spare linear drive unit and pump module which was stored on an external stowage platform on the station\'s truss during one of the spacewalks.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Two satellites were also carried by the orbiter, for deployment when the mission ended. The Dual Autonomous Global Positioning System On-Orbit Navigator Satellite, called DRAGONSAT, gathers data on autonomous spacecraft rendezvous and docking capabilities, and consists of two\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picosatellite" title="Picosatellite">\n        picosatellites\n       </a>\n       , the AggieSat2, and PARADIGM (BEVO-1), which acquire\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GPS" title="GPS">\n        GPS\n       </a>\n       data from a device at NASA and send it to ground stations at\n       <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University" title="Texas A&amp;M University">\n        Texas A&amp;M University\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">\n        University of Texas at Austin\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dragon_18-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dragon-18">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After release, the two picosatellites remained attached for two orbits to collect GPS data, and separated during the third orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A second satellite, the Atmospheric Neutral Density Experiment (ANDE-2), is part of a\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense" title="United States Department of Defense">\n        United States Department of Defense\n       </a>\n       project flown by the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Research_Laboratory" title="United States Naval Research Laboratory">\n        Naval Research Laboratory\n       </a>\n       to provide high-quality satellites, and will measure the density and composition of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Low_Earth_orbit" title="Low Earth orbit">\n        low Earth orbit\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere" title="Atmosphere">\n        atmosphere\n       </a>\n       while being tracked from the ground, to better predict the movement and decay of objects in orbit.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ande_19-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ande-19">\n         [NASA 4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ANDE-2 consists of two spherical\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miniaturized_satellite#Microsatellite" title="Miniaturized satellite">\n        microsatellites\n       </a>\n       , ANDE Active spacecraft (Castor) and the ANDE Passive spacecraft (Pollux), and will be tracked by the International Laser Ranging Service (ILRS) network as well as the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Space_Surveillance_Network" title="United States Space Surveillance Network">\n        Space Surveillance Network\n       </a>\n       (SSN).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ande_19-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ande-19">\n         [NASA 4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One of the satellites, Pollux, is running\n       <a href="/wiki/Arduino" title="Arduino">\n        Arduino\n       </a>\n       libraries, with its payload programmed and built by students.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A set of experiments to be deployed on the ISS were carried by STS-127, namely Dosimetry for Biological Experiments in Space (ESA), Validation of Procedures for Monitoring Crew Member Immune Function, the student-made Image Reversal in Space (\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">\n        CSA\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_University" title="International Space University">\n        ISU\n       </a>\n       ), Nutritional Status Assessment (NASA), NASA Biological Specimen Repository and Tomatosphere-II (CSA).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presskit_4-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-presskit-4">\n         [NASA 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The STS-127 Official Flight Kit (OFK) included water samples from each of the five\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       , a resin statue of a water droplet for the\n       <a href="/wiki/One_Drop_Foundation" title="One Drop Foundation">\n        One Drop Foundation\n       </a>\n       , and a copy of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beethoven" title="Beethoven">\n        Beethoven\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._5_(Beethoven)" title="Symphony No. 5 (Beethoven)">\n        Fifth Symphony\n       </a>\n       for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Montreal Symphony Orchestra">\n        Montreal Symphony Orchestra\n       </a>\n       , among other mementos.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ofk_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ofk-20">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The docking module was also mounted with the DragonEye\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=3D_Flash_LIDAR&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="3D Flash LIDAR (page does not exist)">\n        3D Flash LIDAR\n       </a>\n       ranging system manufactured by\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Advanced_Scientific_Concepts,_Inc.&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Advanced Scientific Concepts, Inc. (page does not exist)">\n        Advanced Scientific Concepts, Inc.\n       </a>\n       . The module was launched to test the docking system which will be used by the commercial\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        SpaceX Dragon\n       </a>\n       re-usable cargo carrier to send supplies to the ISS during the post-shuttle era. The Dragon spacecraft made its successful maiden flight in December 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Location\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Cargo\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Mass\n 6\xc2\xa0k\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bays 4\xe2\x80\x937\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module"       </td>\n        <td>\n         3,946 kilograms (8,699\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bay 13P\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         APC/ECSH\n </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_milestones">\n        Mission milestones\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-127&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mission milestones">\n style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-127_Mission_Poster.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5475" data-file-width="7275" height="166" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/STS-127_Mission_Poster.jpg/330px-STS-127_Mission_Poster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/STS-127_Mission_Poster.jpg/440px-STS-127_Mission_Poster.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-127_Mission_Poster.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Mission poster\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The mission marked:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ql1_1-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ql1-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        158th NASA manned space flight\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        128th Space Shuttle mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        127th shuttle mission since\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-1" title="STS-1">\n         STS-1\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        23rd flight of space shuttle\n        <i>\n         Endeavour\n        </i>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        29th shuttle mission to the ISS\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        102nd post-\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">\n          Challenger\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        14th post-\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">\n          Columbia\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        mission\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1st time that two Canadians have been in space at the same moment\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Shuttle_processing">\n        Shuttle processing\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-127&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Shuttle processing">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2123" data-file-width="3000" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg/220px-STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg/330px-STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg/440px-STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-127_Endeavour_on_Launch_Pad_39A.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\n         </i>\n         at\n         <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n          Launch Pad 39A\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       served as the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-400" title="STS-400">\n        STS-400\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-3xx" title="STS-3xx">\n        rescue\n       </a>\n       vehicle for\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n        STS-125\n       </a>\n       , and was prepared for a possible liftoff from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Launch_complex_39" title="Launch complex 39">\n        Launch Pad 39B\n       </a>\n       on 15 May 2009, four days after the launch of STS-125.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hubble_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hubble-22">\n         [NASA 5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dates_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-dates-23">\n         [NASA 6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       performed the late inspection and was cleared for re-entry,\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       was officially released from stand-by status on 21 May 2009, and preparations for STS-127 were initiated.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FD11a_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FD11a-24">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       moved from Launch Pad 39B to 39A on 31 May 2009 in preparation for STS-127.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-move2_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-move2-25">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-move_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-move-26">\n         [NASA 7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The crew of STS-127 arrived at\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       on 2 June 2009, for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Terminal_countdown_demonstration_test" title="Terminal countdown demonstration test">\n        Terminal Countdown Demonstration Test\n       </a>\n       (TCDT) that concluded with a full launch dress rehearsal.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-move_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-move-26">\n         [NASA 7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mark_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Mark-27">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary.2C_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (August 2009)">\n           non-primary source needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The Flight Readiness Review (FRR), a meeting during which NASA managers assess mission preparations and officially set the launch date, concluded on 3 June 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRR_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FRR-28">\n         [NASA 8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For the first time, live status updates about the FRR were published periodically during the meeting via NASA\'s Twitter stream.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRR_28-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FRR-28">\n         [NASA 8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Launch_attempts">\n        Launch attempts\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-127&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Launch attempts">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-127-2009-3836.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/STS-127-2009-3836.jpg/220px-STS-127-2009-3836.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/STS-127-2009-3836.jpg/330px-STS-127-2009-3836.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/STS-127-2009-3836.jpg/440px-STS-127-2009-3836.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-127-2009-3836.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Close-up view of the Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate on STS-127\'s\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n          external tank\n         </a>\n         during the first maintenance effort\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The launch countdown began 10 June 2009, but on 13 June 2009, as tanking was underway, a gaseous hydrogen leak on a vent line near the Ground Umbilical Carrier Plate was observed, and the 13 June 2009 launch was scrubbed at 00:26 EDT. As liquid hydrogen fuel is pumped in, some of it boils off as the extremely cold liquid enters the warm external tank. The vent line valve controls the resulting buildup of gas pressure by allowing excess gas to escape into a ground-side vent line, which leads to a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flare_stack" title="Flare stack">\n        flare stack\n       </a>\n       at a safe distance away from the pad. A similar leak situation was seen during the first launch attempt of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-119#Shuttle_processing" title="STS-119">\n        STS-119\n       </a>\n       . NASA managers met on 14 June 2009 and 15 June 2009 and evaluated the leak, discussed steps that had to be taken, and set a new launch date of 17 June 2009, at 05:40 EDT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub1_6-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-scrub1-6">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-second_7-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-second-7">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A second launch attempt was made on 17 June 2009 for which NASA moved the planned launch of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter">\n        Lunar Reconnaissance Orbiter\n       </a>\n       to a new date. On 17 June 2009 loading of the shuttle\'s external tank with liquid hydrogen and liquid oxygen was delayed three hours due to poor weather around the launch site, but tanking began once the weather cleared. Approximately two hours after tanking began, engineers saw leak indications in the GUCP similar to those seen during the first launch attempt. The launch was officially scrubbed at 01:55 EDT.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub17_10-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-scrub17-10">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Following the launch scrub, Chairman of NASA\'s Mission Management Team\n       <a href="/wiki/LeRoy_E._Cain" title="LeRoy E. Cain">\n        LeRoy Cain\n       </a>\n       noted that engineers would work to understand the hydrogen leak issue and come up with a solution to the problem. Cain said managers were hopeful that the issue could be resolved in time for the next available launch opportunity on 11 July 2009.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secondscrub_29-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-secondscrub-29">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Due to the delay of STS-127, managers noted that it was likely that the launch of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-128" title="STS-128">\n        STS-128\n       </a>\n       on 7 August 2009, would be pushed back slightly.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-secondscrub_29-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-secondscrub-29">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg/220px-Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg/330px-Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg/440px-Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Space_Shuttle_Endeavour_lightning_strike.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lightning strikes\n         <i>\n          Endeavour\'\n         </i>\n         s Launch Pad.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On 1 July 2009, the shuttle managers conducted a new series of tanking tests to confirm a hypothesis that a misaligned vent port housing was the root cause of the leaks. The existing rigid seal was replaced with a flexible one in the hope that it would maintain a tight fix even under the cryogenic conditions that seem to cause the leak. The test was declared a success with no leaks detected on the GUCP. The mission was announced to be targeting an 11 July 2009 launch.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-special_test_30-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-special_test-30">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-test_success_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-test_success-31">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On the evening of 10 July 2009 the launch pad region was hit by eleven strikes of lightning, which pushed back the 11 July 2009 launch time by at least 24 hours. Two of the strikes were strong enough to trigger an evaluation by NASA engineers. The inspections revealed that no damage had been done to the space shuttle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub4_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-scrub4-32">\n         [NASA 9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA scrubbed\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       \' 12 July 2009 launch attempt at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-minus" title="T-minus">\n        T-minus\n       </a>\n       9 minutes and holding due to Cumulus clouds and lightning near the launch pad. During the final Go/No-Go polls, Mission Control in Houston declared a "No-Go" due to unacceptable weather forecast for a possible Return-To-Launch-Site (RTLS) abort, and planned for emergency scenarios when one or more engines shut down early leaving insufficient energy to reach the Transatlantic Abort Landing (TAL) sites. Similarly, during the 13 July 2009 attempt, RTLS weather was also "no go." Meanwhile, shuttle weather officer Kathy Winters informed the launch director,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pete_Nickolenko" title="Pete Nickolenko">\n        Pete Nickolenko\n       </a>\n       , that the launch pad weather had changed to RED as the Phase-1 Lightning warning was issued for the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       . The launch was scrubbed at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/T-minus" title="T-minus">\n        T-minus\n       </a>\n       9 minutes and holding and was quickly reset for 15 July 2009 (a 48 hours scrub turn around) due to weather concerns on 14 July 2009 and the desire to replace the Tyvek covers over the forward Reaction Control System thrusters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub5_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-scrub5-33">\n         [NASA 10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n     </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         4\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span class="sortkey" style="display:none;">\n          2009-07-12 19:13:55 !\n         </span>\n         <span class="sorttext">\n          12 Jul 2009, 7:13:55 pm\n         </span>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         scrubbed\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0 days, 23 hours, 34 minutes\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         weather\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         (T\xe2\x80\x93 9:00 hold)\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         70%\n         <sup lightning near launch pad\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-scrub4_32-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-scrub4-32">\n           [NASA 9]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n
